1630 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


N.Y. State Ass'n of Tobacco & Candy Distribs. v. City of New York


Index No. 124298/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


3 Misc. 3d 876; 773 N.Y.S.2d 783; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1776



November 6, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motions by defendants to dismiss granted; complaint dismissed; plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction denied; plaintiffs' cross-motion for leave to amend the complaint denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a trade association of tobacco and candy distributors and several tobacco distributors, sued defendants, the City of New York and various city and state officials, seeking an order enjoining city officials from enforcing New York City, N.Y., Local Laws No. 10 (2002), which raised the excise tax on cigarettes sold in the city. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the action. Plaintiffs filed motions as well.


OVERVIEW: A trade group and several tobacco distributors sued the City of New York and city and state officials, claiming that New York City, N.Y., Local Laws No. 10 (2002), which raised the excise tax on a pack of 20 cigarettes sold in the City from eight cents to $ 1.50, violated U.S. Const. amend. XIV and N.Y. Const. art. 1, § 6, and they sought an order prohibiting city officials from collecting the tax. The trial court held that (1) even assuming that the tax was oppressive, it did not violate the Due Process Clauses of the United States or New York Constitutions, and the trade group and distributors' remedy was to seek relief from the legislature, not from the courts; (2) the court would not allow the trade group and the distributors to depose the Mayor of New York City to see if he had an ulterior motive for urging the City to raise the excise tax; and (3) because the trade group and the distributors were unable to demonstrate a likelihood of success on the merits of their claims, the court would not grant their motion for a preliminary injunction.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction, denied plaintiffs' motion for leave to amend their complaint, and granted defendants' motion to dismiss the action.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Tax on Cigarettes and Tobacco Products -- New York City Excise Tax

1. A local law of the City of New York, that raised the excise tax on a pack of cigarettes from 8 ¢ to $ 1.50, did not violate substantive due process. Plaintiffs failed to allege any facts to establish that the law was not designed to further its stated legitimate purposes of raising revenues to close the City's budget gap and deterring smoking by City residents, particularly children. The cigarette excise tax increase enacted by the law had legitimate governmental objectives and a rational basis. "Mixed-motive taxes" may be imposed with the objectives of both raising revenues and deterring a lawful, but disfavored activity, e.g., smoking; nor does a mere high rate of taxation and a stated deterrent purpose render a tax a penalty, where the tax is not imposed on a criminal activity. Moreover, discovery was not necessary to ascertain whether the Mayor, in urging passage of the tax increase, had an alleged "ulterior motive": the complete elimination of smoking.

Taxation -- Tax on Cigarettes and Tobacco Products -- New York City Excise Tax

2. A local law of the City of New York, that raised the excise tax on a pack of cigarettes from 8 ¢ to $ 1.50, did not contravene due process on the theory that it was unreasonably high and, thus, threatened the continued viability of plaintiffs' cigarette distribution businesses within the City. Subject to constitutional inhibitions, the Legislature has very nearly unconstrained authority in the design of taxing impositions. Even a state tax that has the effect of destroying a business must be sustained if it is not invidious. Deterrence of smoking has long been recognized as a legitimate motive for a cigarette tax, and the remedy for an allegedly "oppressive tax" lies with the Legislature, not the judiciary.

 

1631 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hammonds


Indictment No. 03-0845


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, WESTCHESTER COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 880; 768 N.Y.S.2d 166; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1396



October 31, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] People's application granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The People filed an order in the trial court (New York) to show cause requiring defendant to appear in a lineup pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 249.40(2)(b)(i) after defendant was charged with various offenses. Defendant opposed the motion and alternatively requested that the lineup be held in a double-blind and sequential manner, and that a stenographer and photographer record the lineup proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was not good cause for a lineup. The trial court found good cause for the lineup. Defendant's request for a double-blind lineup was denied. The trial court's authority to order that the district attorney employ the sequential and/or double-blind lineup was unsettled, and the trial court was not willing to usurp law enforcement's discretion as long as the procedure was constitutional. The trial court refused to embark on a slippery slope of ruling on future applications based on scientific evidence. Further, given the circumstances of the case, the use of a double-blind sequential lineup would most likely have no impact on the reliability of the identification procedure as the victim had already identified defendant's photograph from a mug shot book. To the extent there had been a misidentification, the damage was irreparable, and the victim would likely again identify defendant in the lineup, whether it be sequential or simultaneous. Given the critical nature of the identification evidence and the apparent weaknesses in the People's case, the People were ordered to furnish a stenographer and photographer to memorialize the lineup proceedings.


OUTCOME: The People's application was granted to the extent that a lineup was ordered. The trial court further ordered the People to provide defense counsel with notice seven days in advance of the date on which the lineup was scheduled to be held, and to furnish the services of a stenographer and photographer to memorialize the lineup proceedings. Defendant's application for a double-blind, sequential lineup was denied.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Identification of Defendant -- Lineup -- Use of Double-Blind or Sequential Lineup 

The People, after being granted an order pursuant to CPL 240.40 (2) (b) (i) requiring defendant's participation in a postindictment lineup, were not required to conduct either a double-blind lineup, in which the law enforcement officers conducting the lineup would have no knowledge as to which of the participants was the true suspect, or a sequential lineup, in which the victim would view each potential suspect separately and then make a determination on each individually without ever viewing all the potential suspects simultaneously. It would have been an improper infringement on law enforcement to have ordered the People to employ either lineup methodology as long the simultaneous, non-double-blind lineup procedure had not been declared unconstitutional. Furthermore, given the critical nature of the identification evidence, the People were ordered to furnish a stenographer and photographer to memorialize the lineup proceedings in order to reduce the opportunity for any unintentional suggestiveness from law enforcement personnel.

 

1632 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. West


Indictment No. 8529/83


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


2 Misc. 3d 332; 768 N.Y.S.2d 802; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1485



October 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 3, 2004. Counsel Amended December 22, 2003.
Reversed by People v. West, 12 A.D.3d 152, 783 N.Y.S.2d 473, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13061 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Nov. 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Sentence vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.20(1), seeking an order setting aside a sentence that was imposed after he was convicted of rape and sodomy in the first degree. He claimed that the procedures used to sentence him as a discretionary persistent felony offender violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution, as interpreted by the United States Supreme Court in its Apprendi decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of rape and sodomy in the first degree, and the trial court which convicted him determined that he had prior convictions for rape, sodomy, assault and battery, and assault with intent to rob, and it used those convictions to enhance his sentence. After the United States Supreme Court issued its Apprendi decision, defendant filed a motion to set aside his sentence, arguing that the procedures which were used to sentence him as a discretionary persistent felony offender violated the Due Process Clause of the United States Constitution. The trial court held that (1) although the Court of Appeals of New York reviewed New York's discretionary offender scheme after the United States Supreme Court issued its Apprendi decision and found in its Rosen decision that the scheme was constitutional, the court's Rosen decision conflicted with the Supreme Court's Ring decision and could no longer be considered good law; and (2) because the court of appeals' Rosen decision conflicted with the Supreme Court's Ring decision, the trial court was not required to follow Rosen and it would vacate defendant's sentence and resentence him.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's sentence and ruled that it would resentence him.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Sentence -- Persistent Felony Offender -- Validity of Discretionary Persistent Felony Offender Procedures

Defendant was entitled to vacatur of the enhanced sentence imposed upon him as a discretionary persistent felony offender because it was based, in part, upon the factual determination of the sentencing judge under a "preponderance of the evidence" standard that defendant's history and character and the circumstances of his criminal conduct justified such enhanced sentencing (CPL 400.20 [5]; Penal Law § 70.10 [2]). The procedures used to sentence defendant as a discretionary persistent felony offender were unconstitutional as violative of due process to the extent that the sentencing judge made factual findings beyond defendant's prior convictions that resulted in the enhanced sentence. The United States Supreme Court has determined in cases subsequent to defendant's conviction that all facts essential to the imposition of the level of punishment that a defendant receives must be found by the jury beyond a reasonable doubt.

 

1633 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Joyner v. N.Y. City Hous. Auth.


Index No. 27553/1992


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 795; 772 N.Y.S.2d 221; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1291



October 20, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Plaintiff's motion to vacate denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party sued defendant housing authority for personal injuries arising from a slip and fall. After the trial court dismissed the injured party's action for a failure to prosecute it, she moved to vacate the dismissal. The housing authority cross-moved to dismiss the matter as abandoned.


OVERVIEW: The injured party failed to provide basic discovery demanded by the housing authority. The injured party also repeatedly did not comply with the trial court's orders to file a note of issue by a date certain. The last time she did not comply with such an order, or appear for a conference with the trial court, her claim was dismissed over five years after she filed it. Six years later, she sought to vacate that dismissal. Under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3216, a dismissal of her case for unreasonably neglecting to proceed could not be ordered unless she was served with a written demand by registered or certified mail requiring her to serve and file a note of issue within 90 days. The housing authority never served such a demand on the injured party. Absent that demand, the trial court had no power to dismiss the action. The trial court had no discretion to consider whether the housing authority would be unduly prejudiced by the delay inherent in reinstating the matter.


OUTCOME: The injured party's motion to vacate the dismissal of her claim, and to give her an opportunity to file a note of issue, was granted, and the housing authority's cross-motion to dismiss her lawsuit as abandoned was denied.


HEADNOTES

Dismissal and Nonsuit -- Want of Prosecution -- Failure to Serve 90-Day Demand 

In a personal injury action commenced more than 10 years ago in which plaintiff failed to comply with several court orders directing her to file a note of issue, but defendant never served plaintiff with a 90-day demand to file a note of issue pursuant to CPLR 3216, plaintiff's motion to vacate the dismissal of her claim and to give her an opportunity to file a note of issue was granted. Under CPLR 3216, a court may not dismiss an action where a party unreasonably neglects to proceed in an action unless the court or party seeking dismissal has served a 90-day demand. Absent such notice, a neglectful plaintiff's lawyer is relieved of the burden of showing that the claim has any merit, or even that a reasonable excuse exists for failing to prosecute an action.

 

1634 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lobianco


Docket No. 2003KN0139 14


CRIMINAL COURT OF THE CITY OF NEW YORK, KINGS COUNTY


2 Misc. 3d 419; 766 N.Y.S.2d 807; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1393



October 14, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 22, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss denied; defendant's motion for reservation of rights granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss, on grounds of statutory vagueness, existence of a legal impediment, and as facially insufficient, an information charging him with criminally possessing a hypodermic instrument in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 220.45. He also moved to reserve his right to make further motions as required.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested after allegedly being observed shooting heroin in public, but due to evidentiary deficiencies, the charge eventually filed was for misdemeanor unlawful possession of hypodermic instruments. The court first held that even though the definition of unlawful under § 220.45 could only be determined by reference to pharmacy regulatory statutes, specifically N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3381, it was not unconstitutionally vague, because it was clear that the penal statute would not be enforced against a possessor whose possession complied with § 3381. There was no legal impediment to the information, because the determination whether defendant in fact bought the hypodermic instruments legally would be a matter for trial. The information was facially sufficient without specifically alleging unlawfulness under § 3381. Finally, the prosecution was mistaken in asserting that defendant would bear the burden of showing his possession was legal, because N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 3396, which shifted certain burdens to defendants in drug-related cases, did not apply to prosecutions under the penal laws.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss but granted the motion to reserve the right to file further motions.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Criminally Possessing Hypodermic Instrument

1. Penal Law § 220.45, which proscribes "knowingly and unlawfully" possessing a hypodermic syringe or needle in violation of article 33 of the Public Health Law, is not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's prosecution for unlawfully possessing two hypodermic needles containing heroin residue. The statute, as written, sufficiently specified the type of behavior considered unlawful so as to eliminate the danger of arbitrary and discriminatory applications. Furthermore, the fact that the statute cross-references article 33 of the Public Health Law does not render the statute unconstitutionally vague.

Crimes -- Criminally Possessing Hypodermic Instrument -- Exception to Criminal Liability for Needles Purchased at Pharmacy

2. The accusatory instrument charging defendant with criminally possessing a hypodermic instrument in violation of Penal Law § 220.45, based upon the arresting officer's observation of "defendant holding in his hand two hypodermic needles containing heroin residue," was facially sufficient for pleading purposes. The statute proscribes "knowingly and unlawfully" possessing a hypodermic syringe or needle in violation of article 33 of the Public Health Law. Although Penal Law § 220.45, by virtue of the Public Health Law definition of the element "unlawful," exempts from criminal liability persons over 18 years old who purchase less than 10 hypodermic instruments from a pharmacy (see, Public Health Law § 3381 [6]), the People were not required to plead in the accusatory instrument that defendant did not purchase the subject needles at a pharmacy. Since the exception to criminal liability is found outside of the Penal Law, it is treated as a proviso, rather than as a true exception, and is not required to be pleaded. However, the People still bear the burden of proving at trial that defendant did not purchase the needles at a pharmacy.

 

1635 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Niksus Realty LLC v. Assessor of Greenburgh


Index Nos.: 15273/01, 16406/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, WESTCHESTER COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 764; 766 N.Y.S.2d 335; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1271



October 7, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reargument granted by, Adhered to Niksus Realty LLC v. Assessor of Greenburgh, 3 Misc. 3d 267, 772 N.Y.S.2d 798, 2004 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 103 (N.Y. Sup. Ct., Feb. 11, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Applications denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer sought an order declaring N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 727, prohibiting a change in an assessment following litigation, inapplicable to proceedings concerning respondent assessor's assessment of his property or, pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 710, an order consolidating the case with another pending case.


OVERVIEW: The property's prior owner reached a settlement with the assessor regarding the property's tax assessment. After the property was transferred to the taxpayer, the applicable equalization rate declined, and the taxpayer sought to apply the lower rate, but such a change was precluded by N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 727. The case was not factually similar to a case in which § 727 was found inapplicable because (1) the subsequent assessment did not exceed constitutional limits, under N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 2, and (2) it was at least arguable that the taxpayer was not wholly unconnected to the property's prior owner, as the taxpayer had been sole shareholder of the property's lessee when the prior owner owned it. Therefore, the case in which N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 727 was found inapplicable was distinguishable, and it was not appropriate to declare § 727 inapplicable to the instant case. The taxpayer's request to consolidate the matter with another case was not appropriate because a settlement of the other case was approved, so there was no other case with which to consolidate the instant matter.


OUTCOME: The taxpayer's motion to find a statute inapplicable to the case was denied, as was his motion to consolidate the case with another case.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment -- Prohibition against Change in Assessment Following Litigation 

Petitioner corporation, which became the owner in December 2000 of property for which the previous owner obtained reduced assessments for calendar years 1996-2000, may not defeat the three-year moratorium period against changing the assessed valuation set forth in RPTL 727 in its attempt to reduce the 2001-2002 assessments. Although petitioner alleged that there was a 27% decline in the equalization rate from 2000 to 2002, which would have caused the property's 2002 assessment to be in excess of its full market value, RPTL 727 does not list fluctuations in equalization rates as one of its stated exceptions. The assessment being challenged was not in excess of constitutional limits, and petitioner, a corporation owned by the same person who owned the corporation previously leasing the property, was not a transferee who had absolutely no connection whatsoever to the assessment reduction at issue. Both of those factors must exist in order to defeat RPTL 727.

 

1636 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cole


Indictment No.867/86


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, CRIMINAL TERM, KINGS COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 531; 765 N.Y.S.2d 477; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1169



September 12, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Cole v. Walsh, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 90128 (E.D.N.Y., Sept. 25, 2009)



DISPOSITION: Motion to vacate the conviction denied.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for vacatur of judgment, wherein he was convicted of manslaughter in the first degree and related charges and was sentenced thereon. His motion sought a new trial based on a claim of newly discovered evidence. He alleged that there were Brady violations and he asserted a free-standing claim of innocence.


OVERVIEW: A man was shot on a street corner and defendant was named as the shooter. He was convicted. The record revealed that others had indicated that defendant was not the shooter and he had an alibi witness as well. Thereafter, defendant filed a motion to vacate the judgment. A hearing was held on the newly discovered evidence claim, as well as on possible Brady violations and a free-standing claim of innocence. Defendant presented four eyewitnesses who indicated that he was not the shooter, as well as a taped recantation of earlier witnesses who had identified him as the shooter. The court found that the evidence was not shown to have been newly discovered, nor was it shown that it was undiscoverable prior to trial if due diligence had been exercised. The court also found that the Brady claims lacked merit because there was no showing that exculpatory evidence which defendant was unaware of had been withheld. The court found that conviction and incarceration of an innocent person violated N.Y. Const. art. 1, §§ 5, 6, and that defendant could claim free-standing innocence. However, the court found that he had not shown such innocence by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to vacate the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Vacatur of Judgment of Conviction -- Newly Discovered Evidence 

1. Defendant, who was convicted of manslaughter in 1987 based on the testimony of two eyewitnesses identifying him as the shooter, is not entitled to a new trial pursuant to CPL 440.10 on the ground of newly discovered evidence. The audiotape and videotape of an alleged recantation by one of the eyewitnesses, and the statement of an uncalled witness that defendant was not the shooter, do not constitute newly discovered evidence. Defendant failed to establish by a preponderance of the evidence that the uncalled witness could not have been discovered with due diligence prior to trial. Defendant was aware that other eyewitnesses had selected other persons as the perpetrator. Furthermore, defendant failed to prove that the People possessed exculpatory evidence that was not turned over to the defense.

Crimes -- Vacatur of Judgment of Conviction -- Free-Standing Claim of Actual Innocence 

2. Defendant, who was convicted of manslaughter in 1987, may raise a free-standing claim of actual innocence as a ground for postconviction relief pursuant to CPL article 440. While the incarceration of an actual innocent person is not violative of the Federal Constitution so long as the jurisdiction provides for a pardon based upon innocence (see Executive Law § 19), the conviction and continued incarceration of an actual innocent person is violative of the New York Constitution. CPL 440.10 (1) (h) provides a basis for vacating a judgment obtained in violation of an accused's constitutional rights. A defendant claiming actual innocence must establish by clear and convincing evidence, considering the trial and hearing evidence and any other reliable evidence whether in admissible form or not, that no reasonable juror could have voted to convict. Here, although defendant demonstrated that he is probably innocent, he failed to meet his burden of proof by the requisite clear and convincing evidence.

Ten's Cabaret, Inc. v. City of New York


Index No. 121197/02, Index No. 122740/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 399; 768 N.Y.S.2d 786; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1163



September 9, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Case Name Corrected January 20, 2004.
Later proceeding at Ten's Cabaret v. City of New York, 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9822 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Sept. 23, 2003)
Later proceeding at Ten's Cabaret, Inc. v. City of New York, 1 N.Y.3d 592, 808 N.E.2d 355, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 96, 776 N.Y.S.2d 220 (2004)
Reversed by, Vacated by, in part, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Complaint dismissed at, in part For the People Theatres of N.Y., Inc. v. City of New York, 20 A.D.3d 1, 793 N.Y.S.2d 356, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3743 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Apr. 12, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Consolidation granted; summary judgment granted to plaintiffs; defendants' cross-motions for summary judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff adult businesses moved in two separate actions for preliminary injunctive relief against enforcement by defendants, the city and certain officials, of New York City, N.Y., Zoning Reg. § 11-113, as amended in 2001, and to consolidate their actions. The city and officials moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Before its amendment, the zoning regulation had placed severe limitations only on those establishments that devoted a substantial portion (judicially interpreted as 40 percent or more of floor space) to adult pursuits, but the 2001 amendment removed the "substantial portion" language. When the businesses challenged the amendment as placing an unreasonable limitation on freedom of expression under the First Amendment and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8, the court noted that while freedom of speech could be limited in the public interest, any limitation had to be narrowly tailored to address the harms to be avoided. While the earlier version of the ordinance had been justified by various studies showing harms caused by proximity to adult businesses, the newer, more stringent limitations could not be justified by that same research. Collateral estoppel did not apply, because earlier cases addressed the earlier version of the statute. The defense claim of laches was mooted by the businesses' success on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court consolidated the actions, denied the city and officials' motion for summary judgment, and granted summary judgment in favor of the adult businesses.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Freedom of Speech--Zoning Amendment Geographically Restricting Adult Entertainment Establishments 

The 2001 amendments to New York City's Zoning Resolution, which removed the phrase "susantial portion" from the definition of "adult establishment," thereby barring businesses containing any adult entertainment from operating within 500 feet of a church or school in areas where adult establishments are otherwise permitted, constitute an invalid exercise of the zoning power to regulate constitutionally protected expression. Defendants failed to make the requste showing that there is a rational basis for the additional restrictions to the zoning ordinance. The preamendment ordinance validly regulated the location of adult establishments pusant to a 60/40 allocation to determine whether a "susantial portion" of a facility was being used for adult entertainment purposes. The 2001 amendments were purportedly intended to address the problem of sham compliance with the 1995 ordinance. However, defendants failed to demonstrate that the 2001 amendments were narrowly tailored to address the adverse secondary effects caused by adult establishments set forth in the 1993 report that formed the basis of the 1995 ordinance. New evidence is necessary to demonstrate a rational basis for the 2001 amendments and that the 60/40 adult establishments are not the appropriately narrow solution to remedy the secondary effects.

 

1638 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Van Allen v. Democratic State Comm. of N.Y.


Index No.: 5888-02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, ALBANY COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 734; 771 N.Y.S.2d 285; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1209



August 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Transferred by Van Allen & Strunk v. Democratic State Comm., 1 N.Y.3d 545, 807 N.E.2d 287, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 4013, 775 N.Y.S.2d 237 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Motions ruled upon.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-party-affiliated voters instituted a declaratory judgment action to challenge the constitutionality of N.Y. Elec. Law §§ 8-302(4) and 8-308(2). The state attorney general moved to intervene and dismiss the complaint. Defendants, the state board of elections and the state Republican committee, also moved to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The voters claimed that the ban on write-in votes under N.Y. Elec. Law § 8-308(2), the limit under N.Y. Elec. Law § 8-302(4) that only voters enrolled with a particular party could vote in that party's primary election, and the voter registration form were unconstitutional. The state attorney general was allowed to intervene and was granted his motion to dismiss as to the attack on N.Y. Elec. Law § 8-308. The court held that the voters' claim in that regard was legally insufficient because they did not attack the ballot access provisions of the law, such provisions were presumptively constitutional, and bans on write-in voting were permissible if the ballot access laws were otherwise constitutional. However, the court declared that N.Y. Elec. Law § 8-302 was unconstitutional to the extent it conflicted with a rule adopted by the Independence Party allowing non-party-affiliated voters to vote in their primary elections. The ruling did not require anything more than allowing those registered to vote without party enrollment to participate in primary elections to nominate Independence Party candidates for the specified public offices.


OUTCOME: The court granted the attorney general's motion to dismiss as to the attack on the statute regarding write-in votes but denied the rest of the motion, denied the motion to dismiss filed by the board of elections, and granted the motion to dismiss as filed by the state Republican party. The court declared unconstitutional the statute limiting voters to voting only in the primaries of the party in which they were registered, with some limitations.


HEADNOTES

Judgments -- Res Judicata -- Constitutionality of Closed Primary System 

1. Plaintiffs, independent voters whose federal action challenging the constitutionality of New York's closed primary system (Election Law § 8-302 [4]) was dismissed, were not barred by the doctrine of res judicata from again challenging the constitutionality of that system in state court. The First Amendment protects a political party's right to invite independents to participate in its primary. At the time the federal court action was decided, no recognized New York political party had adopted a rule opening its primary to independent voters. However, since the Independence Party thereafter adopted a rule inviting those registered to vote without party enrollment to participate in primary elections to nominate Independence Party candidates for certain public offices in conflict with the state law, res judicata did not bar this declaratory judgment action.

Elections -- Write-in Votes -- Constitutional Challenge to Limited Ban on Write-in Voting 

2. Plaintiffs' constitutional challenge to the limited ban on write-in voting in primary and general elections with regard to any person whose name already appears on the voting machine as a nominated or designated candidate for public office (Election Law § 8-308 [2]) is dismissed as legally insufficient. Bans on write-in voting are permissible if the state's ballot access laws are otherwise constitutional. Plaintiffs did not attack the ballot access provisions of the Election Law. Since the unchallenged ballot access provisions are presumptively constitutional, by challenging only the limitation on write-in voting, plaintiffs did not raise a bona fide controversy.

Elections -- Primary Elections -- Constitutionality of Closed Primary System -- Validity of Registration Form 

3. In a declaratory judgment action challenging the constitutionality of New York's closed primary system (Election Law § 8-302 [4]), plaintiffs' constitutional challenge to the voter registration form, which contained a notice that voting in a primary election required enrollment in a political party (Election Law § 5-210 [5] [f]), was dismissed. Even if the notice was incorrect, the form itself did not deprive anyone of a constitutional right to vote in a primary. The proper procedure for remedying any deficiency in the content of the form was a CPLR article 78 proceeding against the administrative body charged with producing the form.

Elections -- Primary Elections -- Constitutionality of Closed Primary System 

4. New York's closed primary system, which requires party enrollment as a prerequisite to voter participation in a party primary (Election Law § 8-302 [4]), is unconstitutional only insofar as it conflicts with a rule adopted by the Independence Party allowing registered voters without any party enrollment to participate in primary elections to nominate Independence Party candidates for certain public offices. The First Amendment protects a political party's right to invite independents to participate in its primary. There is no state interest in conducting a closed primary system sufficient to justify interference with the associational rights of a political party opting for an open primary. Thus, in the absence of a conflict with those rights, there is no state interest sufficient to justify impingement of an independent voter's right to vote in a primary to which they have been invited.

 

1639 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp.


Index No. 5218-03


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, ALBANY COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 272; 764 N.Y.S.2d 577; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1090



August 20, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 14, 2003. Counsel Corrected September 9, 2003.
Appeal dismissed by, in part Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 5 A.D.3d 829, 773 N.Y.S.2d 460, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2234 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the Local Government Assistance Corporation (LGAC) and the Division of the Budget of the State of New York, sought a preliminary injunction to enjoin defendants, the City of New York and the Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corporation (STARC), from issuing bonds or otherwise implementing the provisions of the Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act.


OVERVIEW: Because the City needed to ease the fiscal burden of large bond payments over the next five years, the state legislature passed the Act, which added a new statutory section, N.Y. Pub. Auth. Laws § 3238-a, and which amended an existing statutory section, N.Y. Pub. Auth. Laws § 3240. The Act authorized 30 years of payments and charged LGAC with the task of channeling the payments from a portion of the State's sales tax. Plaintiffs sought to enjoin defendants from implementing the Act on the basis that it involved an unconstitutional multi-year obligation because it had not subjected the annual payments to a referendum or to an appropriation by the legislature. The court denied plaintiffs' motion. N.Y. Pub. Auth. Laws § 3238-a required that payments to the City be made in accordance with N.Y. State Fin. Law § 92-r, which required an appropriation prior to payment. Although the legislature had modified N.Y. Pub. Auth. Laws § 3240(5), it left intact § 3240(3), which required that payments to the LGAC be appropriated. In addition, the City could only assign to STARC what had already been appropriated. Plaintiffs had failed to show that the Act impaired the rights of bondholders.


OUTCOME: The court denied plaintiffs' motion for a preliminary injunction.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act

Plaintiffs have failed to demonstrate that the Municipal Assistance Corporation (MAC) Refinancing Act (L 2003, ch 62, part A4; ch 63, part V), which replaced the $ 2.5 billion in New York City MAC bonds scheduled to become due in 2008 with 30 years of payments by directing plaintiff Local Government Assistance Corporation (LGAC) to pay to the City of New York $ 170 million annually from the Local Government Tax Assistance Fund until 2034 (Public Authorities Law §§ 3238-a, 3240), is facially unconstitutional. Thus, they are not entitled to a preliminary injunction preventing its implementation. The MAC Refinancing Act further authorizes the Mayor of the City of New York to assign any or all of the annual payments received from the Fund to a newly formed nonprofit corporation (the Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corporation [STARC]), which is authorized to issue bonds to the public. The Refinancing Act is not violative of NY Constitution article VII for failing to subject the $ 170 million annual payments to a referendum or annual appropriation by the Legislature. The act requires that payments from the Fund to the City be made in accordance with State Finance Law § 92-r, which requires a legislative appropriation prior to payment. Furthermore, the assignment of the City's payments to STARC is not an unconstitutional gift or loan by the City without a pledge of full faith and credit (NY Const, art VIII, §§ 1, 2). In addition, the act does not unconstitutionally impinge upon pledges to LGAC's bondholders.

Galante v. Ferrara


INDEX NO.: 011238-03


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NASSAU COUNTY


2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1080



August 13, 2003, Decided


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Withdrawn by publisher Galante v. Ferrara, 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1162 (N.Y. Sup. Ct., Sept. 15, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Petition granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After respondent Board of Elections of the County of Nassau (New York) ruled that petitions filed in the office of the Board purporting to designate respondent candidate as the nominee of a particular political party for the office of town councilman were valid, petitioner objector brought an action seeking an order declaring the petitions invalid.


OVERVIEW: The objector claimed that signatures on the designating petitions were rendered invalid by the failure to include, in the witness identification information, the town or city of the subscribing witness, as mandated by N.Y. Elec. Law § 6-132(2). The court found that the town or city in the witness identification information needed to be added beneath the witness's signature prior to filing the designating petition with the Board of Elections. If this information was not provided, the designating petition was not valid. The legislature intended to require strict compliance with the provisions of N.Y. Elec. Law § 6-132(2), and that provision was not unconstitutional. The failure here to furnish the witness's town or city in the witness identification statement before submitting the designating petition invalidated the signatures on that petition.


OUTCOME: The determination of the Board was reversed. The designating petitions were declared invalid, and the Board was ordered not to place the candidate's name on the ballot.

In re Adoption of Robert


Docket No. A-07-03-P


FAMILY COURT OF NEW YORK, ORANGE COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 669; 766 N.Y.S.2d 311; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 994



July 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 3, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner adoptive parents moved to limit a pending hearing, which concerned whether the consent of respondent biological father to the adoption could be dispensed with, to whether the biological father should be equitably estopped from asserting his claim to paternity.


OVERVIEW: The adoptive parents, in support of their motion, cited various cases in which a biological father, seeking to assert his parental rights over a non-biological parent who had assumed the role of father, had been estopped from asserting paternity and seeking custody/visitation with the child. The court distinguished those cases from the present case and denied the motion. The cases cited by the adoptive parents were based on a finding that the best interest of the child required the biological father be equitably estopped from asserting paternity where the father had delayed asserting paternity and where a parent/child bond had developed with the non-biological father. In the statutes regulating adoption, however, the legislature had not included language establishing "equitable estoppel against the assertion of paternity" as a defense against a biological father seeking to contest the adoption, where the biological father had allegedly delayed or failed to assert parental commitment to the child. Rather, the legislature had set forth specific guidelines under which a court had to determine whether consent to the adoption by the biological father was required.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.


HEADNOTES

Adoption - Consent - Unwed Father - Equitable Estoppel

Equitable estoppel may not be invoked by prospective adoptive parents to prevent the unwed biological father of the subject child from asserting his parental rights and withholding his consent to the proposed adoption. The mechanism for adopting is a matter regulated by statute, and neither the applicable statutes nor controlling appellate decisions authorize using equitable estoppel against the assertion of paternity.

Rachel S. v. Annette R.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


FAMILY COURT OF NEW YORK, KINGS COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 760; 766 N.Y.S.2d 307; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 1272



July 17, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner grandparents filed a petition seeking grandparent visitation pursuant to N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 72. Respondent mother moved to dismiss the petition on the grounds that the operative portion of § 72 was unconstitutional and therefore the grandparents lacked standing to bring the instant petition.


OVERVIEW: The child's father was deceased. The child's parents were never married to each other. The mother urged the trial court to find § 72, as applied, unconstitutional. The mother's principle argument was that under § 72 when one parent died both sets of grandparents were given standing to move for visitation. The mother argued that while it might make sense to give the parents of the deceased standing, it made no sense to give both sets of grandparents automatic standing. The mother contended that, as a result, the statute was the kind of sweepingly broad statute previously held unconstitutional by the United States Supreme Court. To meet constitutional muster a nonparent visitation statute had to be applied in a manner that recognized the presumption that fit parents acted in the best interest of their children and that the trial court had to accord some special weight to the parents' own determination. The New York appellate courts had previously held that § 72 could be interpreted to accord deference to a parent's decision. Thus, § 72 properly afforded the mother the appropriate deference, while still giving the grandparents standing to bring a visitation petition.


OUTCOME: The appellate court denied the mother's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Parent and Child -- Visitation Rights of Grandparents 

Petitioner paternal grandparents had standing under Domestic Relations Law § 72 to seek visitation of their deceased son's child who was born out of wedlock. The statute will not be held unconstitutional, as applied, so long as it is applied in a manner that recognizes the presumption that fit parents act in the best interest of their children, and the court accords some special weight to the parents' own visitation determination.

 

1644 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Courtroom TV Network LLC v. State


Index No. 116954/01


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


1 Misc. 3d 328; 769 N.Y.S.2d 70; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 982



July 15, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 4, 2003.
Affirmed by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 8 A.D.3d 164, 779 N.Y.S.2d 74, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8662 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, June 22, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion for partial summary judgment denied; Defendants' motions for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a courtroom television network, sought a declaratory judgment that N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 52, which in part prohibited the televising of judicial proceedings in which a witness might testify, was unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amend. I and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8. The network moved for partial summary judgment, and defendants, the State of New York and the Governor, cross-moved for summary judgment to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The network argued that N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 52 effected an unconstitutional closure of the courtroom by prohibiting audio-visual coverage of trials and that the court should apply strict scrutiny to the statute. The court disagreed. Audio-visual coverage of court proceedings was neither prohibited nor required under the First Amendment. Thus, a court could impose reasonable restrictions on audio-visual coverage, and a rule barring audio-visual coverage of trial proceedings was a time, place, and manner restriction on speech subject to rational basis scrutiny. The record developed during New York's 10-year experiment with televising court proceedings under expired N.Y. Jud. Law § 218 contained ample evidence from which the legislature could rationally conclude that N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 52 advanced the State's interest in fair trials. The legislature could also reasonably find that its legitimate interest in fair trials outweighed the benefits of permitting camera coverage, even on a discretionary basis. The combined effect of New York's statutory scheme demonstrated that, while public access was guaranteed, fair trial rights took precedence when there was a conflict.


OUTCOME: The court denied the network's motion for partial summary judgment, granted defendants' motions for summary judgment, and declared that the statute was constitutional on its face.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Audiovisual Coverage of Judicial Proceedings -- Constitutionality of Ban on Audiovisual Coverage 

 Civil Rights Law § 52, which prohibits audiovisual coverage of trial court proceedings, does not effect an unconstitutional closure of the courtroom in violation of the First Amendment of the United States Constitution. The constitutional right of the press and public to attend court proceedings does not give rise to a constitutional right to televise or otherwise broadcast court proceedings. Rather, a rule barring audiovisual coverage of trial proceedings is a time, place, and manner restriction on speech subject to rational basis scrutiny. Such a rule is constitutional if it is reasonable, promotes "significant governmental interests," and does not unwarrantedly abridge the opportunities for the communication of thought. The Legislature could rationally conclude, following a 10-year experiment with discretionary audiovisual coverage of court proceedings (see Judiciary Law § 218; 22 NYCRR 131.1 [b]), that the statutory ban on audiovisual coverage advances the State's interest in fair trials. Furthermore, there is no broader right of televised access to court proceedings under the State's constitutional guarantee of freedom of speech (NY Const, art I, § 8).

 

1645 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bell


Ind. No. 3610-80


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, CRIMINAL TERM, BRONX COUNTY


3 Misc. 3d 773; 778 N.Y.S.2d 837; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 884



June 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended July 22, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Motion to reargue was granted and, upon reargument, defendant's motion to declare statute unconstitutional as applied to him was granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of kidnapping and related crimes. The trial court sentenced defendant to a term of 20 years to life imprisonment. Upon defendant's release from prison to lifetime parole, pursuant to the New York Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA), N.Y. Correct. Law § 168 et seq., defendant was duly classified as a Level 1 Sex Offender. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of SORA as applied to him and moved for reargument.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his accomplices attempted to rob a man. The man fled, but left his three-year-old daughter behind. Defendant and his accomplices took the child and then concocted a scheme to blackmail the man and his wife. When this effort was foiled, the men were arrested, and the child was recovered without harm. None of defendant's actions in kidnapping the child were done for the purpose of sexual victimization of the child, and there was no assertion that during the period in which she was held for ransom the child was in any way molested or sexually abused. Defendant argued that because the purpose of SORA was to identify and protect the public from sexual offenders and predators - and he was neither - SORA, as applied to him, was an unconstitutional violation of the constitutional guarantee of substantive due process. The court found that to require defendant to register as a sex offender was completely arbitrary and unreasonable. SORA as applied to defendant violated the Equal Protection and the Due Process clauses of both the United States and the New York Constitutions. Therefore, defendant was not properly subject to classification and registration under SORA.


OUTCOME: The motion to reargue was granted and, upon reargument, the motion to declare the statute unconstitutional as applied to defendant was granted. Accordingly, the New York Division of Parole was permanently enjoined from requiring defendant to register, placing him in their special offender unit, or in any other manner treating him as a sexual offender.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Ex Post Facto Law -- Application of Sex Offender Registration Act 

1. Subjecting defendant to the classification and registration provisions of the Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA) because of his conviction of kidnapping in the first degree involving a child (Correction Law § 168-a [2] [a]; Penal Law § 135.25) prior to the enactment of the SORA was not violative of the Ex Post Facto Clause (U.S. Const., art I, § 10 [1]). The Ex Post Facto Clause applies only to penal statutes. Sex offender registration laws are not intended as criminal punishments or enhancements, but are essentially civil in nature. Consequently, application of the SORA to a person convicted of a crime cannot be a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Substantive Due Process -- Application of Sex Offender Registration Act Where Registrable Offense Contains No Sexual Component 

2. The Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA) was unconstitutional as applied to defendant as violative of his right to substantive due process of law, where he was classified and registered as a sex offender because of his conviction of kidnapping in the first degree involving a child (Correction Law § 168-a [2] [a]; Penal Law § 135.25), even though the crime was committed without any sexual motivation or purpose. Application of the SORA implicates a fundamental liberty interest. Defendant demonstrated that his statutorily mandated registration as a sex offender was unreasonable and arbitrary, and bore no rational relationship to the purposes of the statute of protecting the community from the dangers of recidivism by sex offenders and assisting law enforcement in the investigation and prosecution of sex offenders.

Constitutional Law -- Equal Protection of Laws -- Application of Sex Offender Registration Act Where Registrable Offense Contains No Sexual Component 

3. The automatic application of the Sex Offender Registration Act (SORA) to defendant based upon his conviction of kidnapping in the first degree involving a child (Correction Law § 168-a [2] [a]; Penal Law § 135.25), even though the crime was committed without any sexual motivation or purpose, was violative of equal protection. There is no rational relationship between classification and registration of nonsex offenders such as defendant and the otherwise legitimate governmental interests of the SORA. Whenever a defendant is convicted of a registrable offense that does not contain a sexual component, a hearing must be held at which evidence must be presented of some sexual facet to the defendant's actions or motivations sufficient to sustain a classification as a sex offender.

 

1646 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Langevin v. State


Claim No. 95763


COURT OF CLAIMS OF NEW YORK


196 Misc. 2d 809; 763 N.Y.S.2d 730; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 971



June 27, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 15, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Claimants' motion for partial summary judgment denied; cross-motion for summary judgment granted; judgment withheld until the underlying claim wa decided; claimants' cross- motion for leave to amend reply denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After claimants, a psychiatric patient and his guardian, filed a claim for personal injuries against defendant, the State of New York, the State filed a counterclaim for the cost of various services provided to the patient and moved for partial summary judgment. Claimants moved to dismiss the counterclaim and also filed a cross-motion for leave to amend their reply to the State's counterclaim.


OVERVIEW: The patient, who began to complain of pain to his face, jaw, and eye, alleged that his complaint went untreated, that a brain infection resulted, and that he required several surgeries. Claimants sued for damages, alleging negligence and malpractice by the psychiatric center's personnel. The State's answer contained a counterclaim, pursuant to N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 43.03, for the cost of services provided to the patient for a period of several years. The court granted the State's counterclaim, denied claimants' motion to dismiss, and denied claimants' cross-motion for leave to amend. The case on which claimants relied in their motion to dismiss had erroneously concluded that because the "ability to pay" was a condition precedent to liability under the Mental Hygiene Law, the State effectively had no independent cause of action for contribution where plaintiffs were indigent. The State was seeking not contribution but recovery by way of a setoff from an asset of the patient, namely, his underlying personal injury action. Where the State sought recovery against a litigant's assets, the financial ability to pay was not a condition precedent to liability.


OUTCOME: The court granted the State's motion for partial summary judgment on its counterclaim and denied claimants' motions.


HEADNOTES

State - Claim against State - State's Right to Assert Counterclaim for Services Rendered to Claimant at Psychiatric Facility

The State may seek recovery, pursuant to Mental Hygiene Law § 43.03, of payment for the costs of services rendered to claimant, a voluntary admittee at a state psychiatric facility, by way of a counterclaim in claimant's underlying negligence and medical malpractice action. The patient's "ability to pay" at the time the services were rendered is not a condition precedent to the State's statutory and common-law right to seek recovery from an asset of the patient. Furthermore, the proscription against contingent counterclaims is inapplicable where the issues in the underlying action and in the counterclaim are intermingled, and where the prospect of two separate trials would engender confusion, unnecessary expense and a waste of judicial economy.

New York v. Eng'rs Country Club

1648 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


City of Rochester v. E & L Piping, Inc.


INDEX # 1999/12094


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, MONROE COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 572; 764 N.Y.S.2d 514; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 860



June 2, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION: Defendant E&L Piping's motion for partial summary judgment was granted, plaintiff's first cause of action in its second amended complaint was dismissed, and all other applications were denied, without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city sued defendant contractor for breach of contract for not satisfying certain requirements regarding the utilization of minority and women business enterprises. The contractor moved for partial summary judgment dismissing this cause of action.


OVERVIEW: The city alleged the contractor breached the parties' contract when it did not adhere to the city's plan for the utilization of minority and women business enterprises by not hiring enough African-American-owned and women-owned subcontractors. The liquidated damages provision related to this part of the contract was plainly, and grossly, disproportionate to any probable actual harm or loss and was a penalty which would not be enforced. The city did not show any actual damages, at the time the parties entered into the agreement, that would justify, in the event of a breach, the sum allowed under the liquidated damages provision. That sum was not an estimate of the extent of injury the city would suffer, nor did the city's plan set forth any probable actual damages or the extent of injury to the city if the plan's goal's were not met. The argument that the liquidated damages clause was intended to compensate for an abstract loss for past discrimination and to achieve a public benefit was insufficient to show it was an enforceable liquidated damages clause.


OUTCOME: The contractor's motion for partial summary judgment was granted.


HEADNOTES

Damages - Liquidated Damages - Penalty for Contractor's Failure to Comply with Affirmative Action Hiring Plan

The liquidated damages clause of a municipal public works contract assessing a financial penalty on a prime contractor for failing to comply with an affirmative action utilization plan for hiring subcontractors is an unenforceable penalty. The contractual provision for damages in the sum of 125% of any shortfall of the utilization plan is grossly disproportionate to the probable actual harm or loss. Plaintiff municipality failed to demonstrate any probable actual damages that would justify the sum allowed under the liquidated damages provision in the event of a breach. The municipal employees charged with enforcing the plan goals could not state any reason or basis for the calculation of damages or specify the damages caused to the city if a prime contractor failed to satisfy the hiring requirements. Moreover, the fact that the liquidated damages clause is intended to achieve a public benefit is insufficient to render the clause enforceable.

New York v. Dary


No. 02090030


JUSTICE COURT OF NEW YORK, VILLAGE OF WESTBURY, NASSAU COUNTY


2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 656; 2003 NY Slip Op 50939(U)

1650 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


In re Jennifer G.


Docket No. S-05583/98, S-05771/99


FAMILY COURT OF NEW YORK, QUEENS COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 692; 764 N.Y.S.2d 503; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 754



May 30, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by Matter of Jennifer G., 2006 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2136 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Feb. 21, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Statute prohibiting secure detention of PINS declared unconstitutional; respondent remanded to a secure detention facility.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father filed a petition under Article 7 of the New York Family Court Act, N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 111 et seq., seeking to have respondent, his daughter, adjudged a person in need of supervision. The court found the daughter to be a person in need of supervision and adjourned the matter for disposition.


OVERVIEW: The minor daughter had a history of running away while being declared a person in need of supervision and a delinquent. Pursuant to N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act § 720(2), the court could not place the child in secure detention for contempt for violating the court's orders. The court found § 720(2) to be unconstitutional because it improperly infringed upon the court's powers to place the child in secure detention and because the statute was not in the child's best interests. Furthermore, the statute did not violate the provisions of 42 U.S.C.S. § 5633 so that the State would still be able to receive the formula grants under that section.


OUTCOME: The court found the restriction imposed on the Family Court from securing in detention persons in need of supervision who violated a valid order of the court to be unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Infants--Persons in Need of Supervision--Need for Secure Detention--Family Court Act § 720 (2) Unconstitutional 

 Family Court Act § 720 (2), which prohibits a child adjudged to be a person in need of supervision (PINS) from being placed in a secure detention facility for any reason, is unconstitutional as violative of the Family Court's inherent power to punish for contempt any disregard of judicial authority. Family Court, having been granted exclusive subject matter jurisdiction over PINS proceedings (see Family Ct Act § 115 [a] [v]), cannot be deprived of the power to enforce, implement and effect the policy and goals inherent in that jurisdiction. Furthermore, the statute violates the Supremacy Clause of the US Constitution in that it contravenes federal legislation that permits secure detention for a PINS respondent who violates a valid court order (see Juvenile Justice and Delinquency Prevention Act of 1974, 42 USC § 5633 [a] [12] [A]). New York, by accepting formula grants under the federal statute, subjected itself to full compliance with its provisions.

 

1651 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Bazinet v. Kluge


Index No. 110143/01


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 231; 764 N.Y.S.2d 320; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 734



May 29, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Bazinet v. Kluge, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6487 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Apr. 29, 2004)
Reversed by, in part Bazinet v. Kluge, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 29 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, Jan. 6, 2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant Reiser's motion to dismiss cross-claims interposed against him was denied with respect to the claims of malpractice asserted in the Second, Fifth and Eighth cross-claims, and was granted with respect to all other cross-claims.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff attempted buyer sued defendants, the owner and the owner's attorney. The owner filed cross-claims against her attorney for malpractice, gross negligence, breach of fiduciary duty, indemnity, and miscalculation of taxes. The attorney moved to dismiss the cross-claims.


OVERVIEW: The owner was going to sell her cooperative apartment to the buyer. The attorney was representing her in the transaction. The buyer advanced funds for the transaction that the attorney placed in escrow in a bank. However, the parties did not complete the transaction and the owner sold the apartment to another party. The other party also advanced funds for the transaction, which the attorney placed in escrow in the bank. When the attorney sought to withdraw the funds from the bank, the attorney was unable to do so because the bank was closed and in receivership. The attorney was only able to recover about a third of the funds. The trial court denied the motion to dismiss the cross-claims seeking lost interest as a result of the alleged malpractice of the attorney in drafting contracts providing for the escrowed monies to be held in interest on lawyer accounts. Further, the alleged conduct did not approach the standard for gross negligence. Additionally, the claims of breach of fiduciary duty and the claim for indemnity were duplicative of the legal malpractice causes of action. Finally, the claim regarding the calculation of taxes was dismissed, as a refund was obtainable.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss the cross-claims interposed against the attorney was denied with respect to the claims of malpractice, and was granted with respect to all the other cross-claims.


HEADNOTES

Attorney and Client - Malpractice - Deposit of Real Estate Escrow Funds in Bank That Failed Prior to Closings

1. Defendant attorney, who represented the seller in the sale of two cooperative apartments and drafted the contracts of sale, may be held liable in legal malpractice for any loss of monies resulting from depositing, as escrowee pending the closings, $2.7 million in a small bank that failed prior to the closings. The complaint sufficiently sets forth a viable claim that it was malpractice for defendant to have drafted contracts providing that the escrow monies be deposited without protection beyond the $100,000 per account Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation insurance. Plaintiff is entitled to have the opportunity to offer expert opinion that in so drafting the agreements defendant deviated from generally accepted standards for real estate practitioners.

Attorney and Client - Malpractice - Attorneys' Fiduciary Funds - Deposit of Real Estate Escrow Funds in Noninterest Bearing IOLA Account

2. Defendant attorney, who represented the seller in the sale of two cooperative apartments and drafted the contracts of sale, may be held liable in legal malpractice for the loss of interest resulting from his having deposited escrow funds in excess of $2.7 million in a noninterest bearing IOLA account pending the closings. An attorney, acting in a fiduciary capacity, may deposit "qualified funds," "nominal in amount or expected to be held for a short period of time," in a noninterest bearing IOLA account, and may not be held liable in damages because of such a deposit "pursuant to a judgment in good faith that such monies were qualified funds" (Judiciary Law § 497). The complaint herein sufficiently alleges that the significant amounts of monies deposited by defendant as escrowee do not constitute "qualified funds" as defined by the statute.

Domenech v. Goord


Index No. 15671/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, WESTCHESTER COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 522; 766 N.Y.S.2d 287; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 753



May 28, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Domenech v. Goord, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7540 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, July 5, 2005)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Respondents ordered to initiate medical treatment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate initiated a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding seeking (1) an order vacating respondent physicians' decision to deny the inmate treatment for Hepatitis C until he participated in an alcohol and substance abuse treatment program; and (2) an order directing the physicians to start the treatment they prescribed.


OVERVIEW: There was no evidence the inmate was a substance abuser. The Eighth Amendment's Cruel and Unusual Punishment Clause prohibited deliberate indifference to his serious medical needs. This indifference was manifested in the doctors' response to his needs by intentionally denying or delaying access to medical care and intentionally interfering with prescribed treatment. The inmate's diagnosis showed his medical needs were sufficiently serious. He showed the officials and physicians acted with a sufficiently culpable state of mind, as they knew of and disregarded an excessive risk to his health. It was improper to deny the inmate medical treatment without medical justification, and the required drug treatment program was irrelevant for the inmate and provided no medical justification for a continued denial of medical treatment. The officials' policy of requiring participation in drug treatment to receive Hepatitis C treatment, as applied to the inmate, was arbitrary and capricious and resulted in a deliberate denial of medical attention to his serious medical condition in violation of the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The physicians and prison officials were ordered to begin the medical treatment prescribed for the inmate.


HEADNOTES

Prisons and Prisoners - Medical and Surgical Treatment - Denial of Treatment for Hepatitis C

Respondent's policy of requiring prisoners suffering from hepatitis C to enroll in an alcohol and substance abuse treatment (ASAT) program in order to receive medical treatment for their condition is arbitrary and capricious as applied to petitioner, who has hepatitis C but is not abusing drugs or alcohol. To withhold necessary medical treatment from petitioner for his serious medical condition based on his failure to complete an ASAT program that is not medically necessary constitutes a violation of the Eighth Amendment.

1655 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Charles T. Sitrin Health Care Ctr., Inc. v. State


Index No. 2002-708, RJI No. 32-02-0890


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, ONEIDA COUNTY


195 Misc. 2d 824; 761 N.Y.S.2d 452; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 518



April 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 2, 2003.Case Name, Counsel and Opinion Amended May 23, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment for defendant was granted on all causes of action, and complaint was dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff charitable organizations moved for summary judgment granting them relief from a gross receipts assessment issued by defendant State and its officials. The State cross-moved to dismiss the complaint. The issue was whether N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2807-d(2)(b)(vi) (2002) repealed a tax exemption enjoyed by charitable corporations, thus violating N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The nonprofit organizations were hospitals pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2801. The nonprofit organizations claimed that by applying the assessment to charitable entities, the statute effectively, but unconstitutionally, repealed one or more exemptions. Although the assessment imposed by N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2807-d (2002) was a tax on the nonprofit organizations' income, it was not an unlawful tax on a tax-exempt entity, since the nonprofit organizations did not fall within any exemption to the assessment imposed by § 2807-d. The court held it could not construe a policy that protected charitable corporations from taxation as giving protection to the charitable organizations at issue absent a specific constitutional or statutory enactment of that policy. There was no constitutional provision which provided a general exemption for charities from taxation. The charitable organizations failed to specify any tax exemption rooted in a general law which was effectively repealed by § 2807-d(2)(b)(vi) and thus did not establish beyond a reasonable doubt that the assessment violated N.Y. Const. art. XVI, § 1.


OUTCOME: The constitutional validity of the statute was upheld. Summary judgment for the State was granted on all causes of action and the complaint was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Health - Nursing Homes - Constitutionality of Assessment on Gross Receipts

The imposition of a six percent assessment on the gross receipts of residential health care facilities (Public Health Law § 2807-d [2] [b] [vi]) does not repeal a statutorily enacted tax exemption granted to plaintiffs, nonprofit nursing homes, and therefore does not violate the constitutional prohibition against repealing tax exemptions extended by general laws to the real or personal property of charitable organizations (NY Const, art XVI, § 1). Plaintiffs have failed to demonstrate the "statutory source of the claimed exemption" that is allegedly being repealed. Although plaintiffs are exempt from certain taxes, such as income, franchise and sales taxes (see 26 USC § 501 [c] [3]; Tax Law §§ 208, 1116 [a] [4]; 20 NYCRR 1-3.4 [b] [6]), there is no statutory prohibition on the imposition of a gross receipts tax. The State's "policy" favoring the exemption from taxation of charitable institutions does not constitute an exemption from a specific tax created by a general law.

 

1656 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Walters


Indictment No. 4472/2002


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


196 Misc. 2d 78; 763 N.Y.S.2d 715; 2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 602



April 23, 2003, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Defendant's motion to dismiss SI(1) was denied. Defendant's motion to dismiss SI(2) was denied without prejudice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, indicted for first degree sexual abuse and related crimes against a child, moved to dismiss two special informations, informing the trial jury that the victim was under 15 and that defendant was previously convicted of a sexual offense against a child, claiming that the special informations authorized by New York's child sex offender statute, N.Y. Penal Law § 70.07, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's indictment was accompanied by two special informations pleading that the victim's age was under 15 and that defendant was previously convicted of a sex crime against a child, exposing him to an enhanced penalty. The Sexual Assault Reform Act, N.Y. Penal Law § 70.07, and N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law §§ 400.19(2) and 200.62 allowed this procedure, and it complied with the requirement that a fact increasing a crime's penalty beyond the prescribed statutory maximum had to proved beyond a reasonable doubt to a jury. If defendant controverted the victim's alleged age, as stated in the special information, that allegation had to be proved to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt, under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 200.62 and N.Y. Penal Law § 70.07. The grand jury did not have to pass upon the victim's age, nor did the age have to be pleaded in the indictment. N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 200.62 and N.Y. Penal Law § 70.07, with the indictment and bill of particulars, gave defendant the required specific notice of the charges against him. Defendant's challenge to the special information alleging his previous conviction of a sex crime against a child was premature, as he had not been convicted.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sex Offenders--Enhanced Sentencing for Repeat Child Sex Offenders--Use of Special Information to Plead Victim's Age Constitutional

In defendant's prosecution for first degree sexual abuse for having subjected the victim to "sexual contact by forcible compulsion" (Penal Law § 130.65), the People were not required to instruct the grand jury regarding the victim's age as an element of the crime before filing a special information pursuant to CPL 200.62 for enhanced sentencing purposes. New York's enhanced sentencing scheme for repeat child sex offenders authorizes the victim's age to be pleaded by special information whenever a person is charged with a sex offense for which the victim's age is not an element of the offense. Under the statutory scheme, the victim's age, unless conceded by the defendant, must be proved to the jury beyond a reasonable doubt. A factual finding by the jury that the victim is under 15, coupled with a determination that the defendant was previously convicted of a child sex offense, subjects the defendant to an enhanced penalty for the present crime (Penal Law § 70.07 [4] [e]; § 70.06 [3] [d]), as well as to an enhanced penalty for any future child sex crime. The use of a special information as a means of submitting the victim's age to the trial jury does not violate federal or state constitutional requirements.

Montemarano v. Serio


Index No. 120239/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, NEW YORK COUNTY


2003 N.Y. Misc. LEXIS 267; 2003 NY Slip Op 50653(U)



March 27, 2003, Decided

Related proceeding at Montemarano v. Atlantic Express Transp. Group, Inc., 123 A.D.3d 675, 997 N.Y.S.2d 700, 2014 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8337, 2014 NY Slip Op 8408 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, 2014)
